If it were true, it would not be only a rewriting of History. It would be an awakening.
At first I was skeptical.
Official dating seemed to refute such longevity of the structures…
How could materials subject to atmospheric erosion, earthquakes, and time itself, remain intact for so long?
For a moment I stopped, torn between rationality and intuition.
But then I remembered a fundamental truth:
when multiple anomalies point in the same direction, they are no longer anomalies.
They are a signal.
I examined the list of sites, observed their orientation, compared them with the hypothesized polar longitudes:
in particular the longitudinal line 47.1°, along which, according to Buildreps, the past poles would have been arranged.
It didn’t take long for me to feel that push of obsession again.
I opened Google Earth, traced the poles, mapped every datum.
Then I carried out one of the operations I loved most: shifting in time.
I ideally repositioned the Greenland plate to its original coordinates in Pangaea, about 195.5 million years ago.
That’s when it happened. The new light-blue polar-connection line, the one traced on the poles proposed by Buildreps (in yellow), no longer followed the longitude 47.1°, but aligned perfectly with the Prime Meridian: 0°.


For an instant, everything seemed to waver.
Was it an error? Or was I looking in the right direction, but with the wrong lens?
The new configuration revealed an angular discrepancy with respect to the coordinates of the plate on which Pangaea’s North Pole lay. While the modern line of the poles under analysis continued in a straight line toward the current North Pole, the version backdated to 195.5 million years did not match by about 640 km.
Craving logical justifications, I tried to calculate the probable incidence of the “crustal tipping” suggested by the astonishing “Equators of Hellas Planitia” and discovered that the effect (highlighted by the yellow dashes indicated above by the arrows ↑) was precisely equal to the distance and angulation needed to cancel the discrepancy.
Once again, the analogies between Earth and Mars proved too precise to be random.
Every time I drew lines, calculated angles, studied inclinations, the truth became clearer.
The fact that hundreds of ancient monuments appeared aligned to precise coordinates confirmed something disruptive:
that the Earth’s ancient memory was not only written in fossils or sediments…
but engraved in stone, with the intent of lasting beyond time itself.
And even if some of Buildreps’ chronological hypotheses still appeared disconnected or premature, they nonetheless represented an important tile in a larger mosaic, one of those that cannot be observed up close… but only from an eagle’s flight.

Chapter 33 — The Broken Axis

A new line had just been drawn in my mind.
Like a sudden flash, it carried with it a meaning buried beneath centuries of hypotheses and silences: the obliquity of the ecliptic — the Earth’s axial tilt relative to its orbital plane.
An apparently technical detail, and yet it was revealing itself as the key to an entire cosmic narrative.
After establishing that the Mount Tai/Nazca trajectory of the Rendlesham Meccano Circuit was perfectly perpendicular to the ecliptic, I understood that I had to dig deeper.
It was time to go back. Not only in time, but into the forgotten history of science.



And so I found myself opening one of the most overlooked works of twentieth-century astronomy: the research of George F. Dodwell, official astronomer of the Adelaide Observatory.
During his research, he discovered the book Draysonia by the British admiral Sir Algernon F. R. DeHorsey, which presented an astronomical theory advanced by Major General Professor Alfred Wilks Drayson.
Drayson, professor at the Royal Military Academy in Woolwich for fifteen years and astronomer at the Royal Observatory in Greenwich for two years, argued for the existence of a “second pole of precession” that influenced the Earth’s motions, thus explaining past geological climates and ice ages.
Aware that Drayson’s theory was considered a paradox by the astronomical authorities, Dodwell decided to critically examine the ancient and medieval observations of the obliquity of the ecliptic on which Drayson based his conclusions.
Such observations, dating back to Strabo, Proclus, Ptolemy, and Pappus, showed a growing divergence from the values calculated using Newcomb’s formula for the secular variation of obliquity.
Dodwell adopted Sir George Airy’s principle, which states that all observations, corrected for known errors, should be used to form an average result, balancing extremely high and low observations.
Dodwell’s method involved:
1. Collecting as many observations as possible of the obliquity of the ecliptic.
2. Correcting each observation for any known errors.
3. Plotting a curve that linked all the observations and comparing it with modern observations.
Through this methodology, Dodwell sought to uncover new truths or circumstances revealed by historical observations. He wrote numerous chapters, from the third to the tenth, in Astronomical Investigations on the Obliquity of the Ecliptic (the initial title later modified), gathering information from ancient civilizations such as China, India, Egypt, and Greece, as well as from medieval Europe and parts of Asia.
A crucial element of his research was the acquisition of the lost manuscript of Godefroid Wendelin, a medieval Belgian astronomer, found in the Library of Bruges and published in 1933.
This manuscript contained a list of ancient observations of the obliquity of the ecliptic and Wendelin’s theory on the cause of the changes observed up to his time.
In 1934, Dodwell plotted the first curve of the ancient observations, finding a progressive anomaly relative to Newcomb’s formula.
This suggested an unknown movement of the Earth in the past, not explainable as a continuous cyclical or periodic motion.
To investigate further, he plotted a curve of the “residuals” (differences between observations and Newcomb’s formula), discovering that the residuals followed a “logarithmic sine curve” indicating a sudden shift of the Earth’s axis in 2345 BC and a return toward equilibrium completed in AD 1850.
Dodwell verified that every point of the mean observational curve corresponded exactly to a point on the logarithmic sine curve, mathematically confirming the hypothesis of an impact that had deflected the Earth’s axis in 2345 BC and the subsequent partial recovery of the Earth over the following 4194 years.
He sent a preliminary paper to the Royal Astronomical Society in 1935, receiving feedback suggesting that he reconsider the errors in the ancient observations.
Following this advice, Dodwell built and tested a vertical gnomon for solstitial observations, confirming the accuracy of the ancient observations within one or two arcminutes and demonstrating that careful observers did not make large errors across long series of observations.
Afterwards, Dodwell devoted himself to an in-depth study of the Solar Temples of Egypt, Stonehenge in Great Britain, and the Solar Temple of Tiahuanaca in Peru.
These ancient monuments, oriented toward the sunrise and sunset points during the summer and winter solstices, supported the results of the Chinese, Hindu, and Greek astronomical observations, reinforcing the conclusions drawn in the previous chapters of his work.
Despite the promising prospects, the publication of Dodwell’s work, intended to be distributed to other observers and examined by astronomers, suffered a suspicious delay.
Nonetheless, his research provided me with a solid foundation for understanding the periodic variations of the obliquity of the ecliptic and the interaction between astronomical theory and historical observations.
Rereading his magnificent work, I was glad to highlight a few passages:
“… If the curve of the ancient observations is extended backward, it becomes steeper and, around the year 2045 BC, it indicates an obliquity value greater than 25 degrees. 
This is one degree higher than the value given by Newcomb, which is 23 degrees, 55 minutes and 55 seconds. Finally, in the year 2345 BC, the curve becomes exactly vertical and indicates a probable value of about 26.5 degrees…”

Chapter 34 — Temples of Light

It was while I was re-examining the coordinates of the Solar Temple of Amon-Ra at Karnak that I understood how obvious the connection was between sacred architecture and planetary inclinations.
The two lines that formed a perfect 90° angle inside the temple started from 25° 11' 24" (25.19°), which corresponds to Martian obliquity, and from the Azores at 37.20° -25.60°, almost coincident with the latitude and longitude of the Portara of Naxos, with the longitude sign inverted.


Moreover, continuing along that same angle, the line that runs from the Azores to Karnak
carried on all the way to the Maldives (-0.86° 73.88°).
Finally, after calibrating the sites with perfect precision, I ran into yet another “coincidence”: starting (toward 74.05° East) from the Azores coordinates—just verified as perfectly aligned with the Temple of Karnak the line passed directly through the Portara of Naxos (already examined for its intersection with the Hellas Planitia Equator and included among the Rendlesham coordinates) and, continuing at the same angle, reached another place of enormous interest, famous for its gigantic and mysterious artifacts: Baalbek.
That was where I received the next confirmation: temples were not merely buildings, but astronomical instruments.
And if they were instruments, then they were measuring something real—something tangible.
The Sun, the seasons… or perhaps the inclination of the entire world.
Dodwell had already said it all, many decades earlier. His words rang out with force:
“… The rays of the Sun, rising or setting on important dates, would have shone down the avenue, striking the image of the Sun God.
In the great Temple of Karnak, this happened at sunset on the day of the summer solstice …”
In 2045 BC, the temple’s foundation date, the Sun’s solstitial declination was 25° 9' 55".
A value almost identical to Mars’s current tilt, and more than a degree higher than what Newcomb’s formula would predict.
It couldn’t be an error. It was a deliberate measurement.
A fixed point from which to measure the Earth’s misalignment.
Baalbek, too, fitted into that network—using the Greek Portara of Naxos as a sight to lock onto the exact point of the Azores aligned with Karnak.
Sacred geography was revealing itself as a geodetic grid.
And then the final revelation:
the pre-slip Hellas Planitia Equator—which I had already associated with an ancient symmetry between Earth and Mars—crossed Giza, Nazca, Machu Picchu, Angkor, Petra, Mohenjo-daro, Tiahuanaco, the Andes, the Thar Desert…
As if a forgotten civilization had pressed into the planet the coordinates of celestial memory.
Dodwell himself, with his calm British precision, confirmed it:
“… It is probable that the Earth’s axis of rotation was altered by the force of an impact in 2345 BC, passing from an original inclination of about 5° to a new inclination of about 26.5° …”
A variation of 21.5°.
Almost identical to the Martian crustal slippage I had measured: 21.28°.
A 1% difference. Too exact to be accidental.
I sat down. I breathed.
Further confirmations for other points on the curve came from the famous solar monuments of Stonehenge, in England, and Tiahuanaco in Peru.
I remembered Dodwell’s words:
“… The vast movements and changes that occurred at the moment of the impact, and which extended their consequences through the centuries that followed, are unimaginable, for they involve both the external and internal state of the Earth.
However, we can note the compatibility of the phenomenon with Jewish traditions and with the statements of Halley and Pierre-Simon Laplace …”
…Before returning to the analysis of data and distances, I couldn’t resist recognizing my favorite manifesto—spoken by an inspired Laplace in 1814—which now struck me as the very description of the “Code” I was deciphering:
“… We may regard the present state of the universe as the effect of its past and the cause of its future. An intellect which, at a given instant, knew all the forces that set nature in motion and all the positions of all the objects of which nature is composed—if such an intellect were also vast enough to analyze these data—would embrace in a single formula the movements of the greatest bodies in the universe and those of the smallest atoms; for such an intellect nothing would be uncertain, and the future, like the past, would be present before its eyes …”
I was a small—tiny—intellect. But I was beginning to glimpse the formula.
Returning to the matter, I recalled that the axial inclination Dodwell attributed to Earth at the time Karnak was built (25° 9' 55'') was, to 99.9%, equivalent to Mars’s current inclination—while the maximum tilt of about 26.5°, which he indicated for 2345 BC, matched 99% of my value of 26.77°.
Another point worth reflection was the minimum inclination he proposed—5°—which would correspond to a planet without seasonal variation, where only the central belt would enjoy a constantly temperate climate. In essence, a kind of circumscribed “Eden.”
Regarding the crustal slippage of 21.28° measured at polar latitude,


I noted again that the inclination obviously follows the “rail” (perpendicular to the planetary orbit) of 17,327.4 km that connects Nazca to Mount Tai. Consequently, the maximum displacement (23.62°) occurred along this vertical line.
Therefore, the farther one moved away from the Nazca/Mount Tai axis—shifting along the polar-slip axis-the more the distance traveled by the planetary crust progressively decreased, until it reached zero near the slip axis itself.
But what truly stole my breath was discovering that the Galactic Equator—
the invisible plane around which the solar system rotates—followed the exact same trajectory as the Mount Tai–Nazca line.
I understood then that I was looking at a plane of universal symmetry, a mirror between:
• the axes of planets
• the orbits of stars
• the intentions of the ancient builders
It was no longer only a geological or astronomical investigation.
It was the map of an intelligence that had inscribed into time and space the traces of an original balance.
I thought of Dodwell. Of his courage. Of his marginalization.
He had been heard—but not believed.
“… Otherwise they would have lobotomized him and named him President …”
I smiled bitterly. Because I knew it was true.
Like Snider-Pellegrini, Plato, Ignatius Donnelly, and all those who had dared to claim that the Earth had not always been as it is now.
As for me—I no longer had any doubts.

Chapter 35 — The Voices of Disorder

When I first read Immanuel Velikovsky, I had the feeling of listening to a voice coming from a side corridor of history: not the main hall of science, but a lateral passage, full of echoes.
I wasn’t interested in believing him.
I was interested in understanding why his mind had ended up there.
Velikovsky spoke of Worlds in Collision. Not as metaphor, but as cosmic chronicle: Venus, according to him, had not “always existed” as it is; it would have been expelled from Jupiter in a catastrophic event, a birth of fire, and then launched into the inner system like a wandering body — a divine projectile.
And in that passage, he said, it would have brushed the Earth.
Tsunamis. Earthquakes. Eruptions. Sudden darkness.
Not symbols: deformed memory. Myths as records, not as fables.
I did not need to accept that mechanics literally — the idea of a planet “born” from another and able to pass close to Earth without annihilating it clashes with physics like a nail against glass.
But the point was not plausibility. The point was the approach.
Velikovsky did something that science, out of prudence, tends to avoid: he joined what is normally kept separate. Astronomy, mythology, history, religion, geology. In the middle of that chaos he searched for recurrences, patterns, cycles. He searched — even if he did not call it that — for a geometry of trauma.
And the unsettling thing was that many of his time windows seemed to graze the knots I had already encountered elsewhere: the anomalies, the discrepancies, the moments of maximum orbital disorder. They did not always coincide. But they called to each other. 
As if more people, from different eras, were touching the same elephant in the dark — each grasping a part.
Then another name emerged, different, older, almost nineteenth-century in its aura: Charles Étienne Brasseur de Bourbourg. A missionary, yes. But above all a linguist. And — rare thing — a man willing to take seriously what the world called “folklore.”
It was he who brought to light the Popol Vuh, and who pursued the buried meanings in Mesoamerican codes when Maya writing was still an unfathomable enigma. In that gesture there was something that struck me more than the theory: a mental posture.
Brasseur did what almost no one does with the defeated: he did not turn them into ethnographic decoration. He treated them as witnesses.
For him, the stories of floods, cosmic cycles, destructions and rebirths were not fantasy: they were history in disguise, filtered through myth because only in that way could it survive. Without GPS, without satellites, without numerical models, he had nonetheless intuited something essential: that certain civilizations do not “invent” identical catastrophes for pure narrative taste. They remember them.
And inevitably Graham Hancock arrived. A modern bridge between fragments.
His explorations of global megalithic sites — from Giza to Göbekli Tepe, from the Andean plateau to the most remote islands — did not appear to me as simple provocations: they were attempts to recompose a broken map.
Hancock insists on an idea: an advanced civilization, prior to official chronologies, erased by a global cataclysm at the end of the last ice age.
Whether he is right in every detail or not, what matters is that his question coincides with mine: where does the precision come from?
Why do certain places seem to speak the language of the stars?
Why are certain architectures more like instruments than monuments?
Thinking back, I saw them all as temporal antennas: Velikovsky, Dodwell, Brasseur, Hancock… each in his own way, each with his errors and his obsessions, intent on picking up weak signals amid the noise of the world.
Perhaps none of them possessed the entire design.
But all of them were looking toward the same fissure.
And me? I was doing only what they could not do all the way to the end: connecting the dots with today’s tools. Data, satellite images, geophysical models, digital archives. 
An external memory, finally vast enough to hold connections that before remained isolated intuitions.
Because if we stop to look with different eyes, the universe speaks.
In temples. In myths. In stars. In poles that migrate.
And in disorder — right there — the most honest trace of what really happened may be hiding.
Everything is connected.
And every tile, even the strangest one, could be the keystone of a larger design: a cosmic symphony that does not ask for faith, but for listening.

Chapter 36 — The Reverse Point

Among the many oddities I encountered along my path, there was one which, however insignificant it seemed at first, kept disturbing me like an insistent echo in Martian silence.
I had spent countless hours digitally flying over barren Martian landscapes, observing craters, fractures, ancient lava flows now fossilized.
And yet, in that specific place—25.419359° latitude and 166.7145° longitude—something seemed to… move.


Not that it truly moved. But it was as if the perspective flipped under my eyes.
An optical illusion, perhaps—and yet repeated with such precision that I began to suspect that behind that effect there was something more.
After months of observations and comparisons, I decided to christen that phenomenon: I called it “Reverse.”
It was as if the rock emerging from the ground swapped with what was buried, as if an invisible mechanism inverted the scene and then returned it exactly as it was before.
A cyclical, silent pulsation—and… unsettling.
Driven by curiosity—and by that sensation I had learned to recognize as a “precursor of something”—I took the coordinates and began tracing their links.
That was when everything took a different turn.
Those coordinates were not isolated.
They were exactly the intersection between the lines that connected Hi-Brasil to the North and South Poles, and those that went from Mount Tai to Easter Island.
An invisible cross, imprinted on the geography of Mars, but mirrored in that of the Earth.



One numerical detail did not go unnoticed.
The longitude of the Reverse point was exactly 1.5 times the Code:
1.11143 × 1.5 = 1.667145.
I felt as if I were reading a ciphered passage in the very fabric of spacetime.
I then decided to rotate the geoid by 180 degrees.
I wanted to discover what lay exactly at the antipodes of Reverse.
As soon as I saw the new coordinates, my blood ran cold: -25.419359°, -13.2855°.
And there, at that remote point, lay the South Atlantic Anomaly.
The South Atlantic Anomaly The Key for a Possible Geomagnetic Reversal  an area known to scientists for being the key to a possible geomagnetic reversal.

A “hole” in the Earth’s magnetic field, slowly expanding like a crack in the planet’s invisible shell. I read everything I could find.
NASA missions. ESA data. Academic articles. Paleomagnetism. Tectonic anomalies.
Everything pointed in the same direction: Something under the South Atlantic Ocean was moving. Something big. Deep. Uncontrollable.
Moreover, that point was strategically positioned right at the center of the African and South American tectonic plates. 
I also observed that the “tangents of the geomagnetic reversal”, which passed exactly through the sites of Mount Tai, Easter Island, and the Boha geoglyphs (located exactly at the antipodes of Easter Island), intersected perfectly, at those coordinates, with the current “Hellas Planitia Equator” and the pre-slip crust equator.
The coincidence became unsettling: the antipodal point of Reverse on Mars—the illusory rock formation—was directly aligned with a potential geomagnetic reversal node on Earth.
And it wasn’t over.
That point fell exactly between the African and South American tectonic plates.


A fissure. A portal. An open suture in the mantle.
A node. A hub. A point where the worlds mirrored each other.
At that point, I no longer had any doubts.
Once again, what I was observing was not random. It was a code.
A signal impressed into the very shape of the planets.
An invitation—or perhaps a warning—left by those who, before us, had read these same patterns… and perhaps vanished precisely because of it.

Chapter 37 — The Expansion Center

I was brooding over yet another enigma when a sudden intuition pushed me to return to the coordinates of the “Reverse” point.
I had the clear sensation that I had overlooked a fundamental detail—something obvious that, however, had hidden itself in the noise of the data.
I opened the Google Earth application specialized on tectonic plates.
And that was when it happened again: a surprise was waiting for me in the ocean. There, in the abyss of the Pacific, I discovered a symbol—a pink triangle, discreet but impossible to ignore.


That point marked the oldest and most significant “Expansion Center” of the Earth’s oceanic plates.
According to the chronological scale, it dated back to about 180 or perhaps 200 million years ago.
An eternity that suddenly showed itself before me, crystallized into a geometric sign on the seafloor.
I realized that that area might not simply be a geological archive, but the very point of origin of the processes of expansion of the Earth’s crust.
A forge of tectonic cycles. And perhaps, also a crucial node for understanding crustal slippage and the movements of the geomagnetic field.
I gave that place a new name, symbolic, solemn: the Center of Terrestrial Expansion.
That concept, so charged with resonances, echoed the theories—which I had just studied—according to which the dimensions of our planet would not be fixed.
A bold hypothesis—and yet, now, increasingly plausible.
By joining old intuitions and new data, the entire reading of terrestrial dynamics kept reconfiguring itself before my eyes.
That center, I thought, could be the keystone for understanding unsuspected connections: between oceanic depths and continental drifts, between the pulsations of the crust and the broader breaths of the planet.
I saw in the Earth not only a celestial body in evolution, but a cyclical being, endowed with its own vital rhythm. It grew. It renewed itself.
The oceanic crust of the Pacific, more than elsewhere, embodied this dynamic. Always young, always in formation. And precisely because it was incessantly destroyed and regenerated, it appeared recent despite its apparent antiquity.
The mechanism was clear:
the crust was born from the ridges, like the East Pacific Rise,
then it migrated, aged, and finally sank into the trenches,
trenches that surround the entire ocean in the infamous Ring of Fire: the Mariana Trench, the Japan Trench, and the Peru–Chile Trench.
Each stretch of crust was pushed down, into the mantle. Recycled. Erased and rewritten like a planetary magnetic disk. The Pacific crust, thus, was always new.
I already knew it: no portion exceeded 200 million years.
I measured that the centroid of this curious triangle was located approximately at 13.063° latitude and 159.573° longitude.
And then, a cartographic intuition struck me like lightning.
I traced an ideal circle, centered on the pink point. A radius of 24.5°. The result was surprising: that line seemed to describe an invisible rail, along which it was possible to simulate Martian crustal slippage.
It was not just a theory. It was a geometric mechanism, working.
In fact, by tracing the line of its “equator” (10,000 km) from any point of the rail and/or circle and then moving it along the virtual trace as if it were the tip of a compass, the path of the “tip” followed perfectly the angle of the crustal slippage and the corresponding poles across the entire geoid.
This method allowed me to visualize how the circle model incredibly represented the “rail” to simulate crustal movements, highlighting the interconnections between Earth and Mars (and the Moon) in a geodetic context and providing a practical scheme for understanding the possible phases of planetary crust displacement along a predetermined axis.
Even the so-called Rendlesham Meccano Path, with its enigmatic angular precision, was a coded echo of this same pattern.
I checked and rechecked, then confirmed the data.
The North Pole, over the span of about 195–200 million years, had migrated by 26.8°. Exactly the same polar-radius difference between Earth and Mars.
A coincidence? No. Not anymore. It was a code.
And as often happened in these moments of revelation, something beneath the surface seemed to respond.
Under that tectonic center, in the deepest belly of our planet, the buried remains of the mysterious geoid Theia were hiding. I had already intuited its presence.
But now I almost felt it pulsing.
Recent studies spoke of enormous “blobs” of dense material, resting near the boundary between the mantle and the core. Silent, but cosmically eloquent.
According to some theories, they were what remained of the protoplanet that, impacting the primordial Earth, had given rise to the Moon.
And I… I was there, reading in faults and depths the surviving traces of that primordial event, which brought me back to the simulated orbits on the Giza plateau…
It was not only geology. It was cosmic archaeology.

Chapter 38 — The Smoking Gun

By now I sensed I was close to the “smoking gun,” that is, the conclusive proof of the “artificial” planetary connections.
Adding new investigative cues (and pushing me in the right direction) was also the research by David E. Smith, Vishnu Viswanathan, Erwan Mazarico, Sander Goossens, James W. Head, Gregory A. Neumann, and Maria T. Zuber, published in September 2022 by the American Astronomical Society.
In the study, the team analyzed the effects of numerous meteoritic impacts on the lunar surface and concluded that, over the course of millions of years, the obliquity of the ecliptic had undergone an overall variation of about 10°.
In other words, the “old” lunar polar coordinates were 80° N/S 0/180° E.



Analyzing the data, it was evident that the formation of the enormous Aitken Basin at the South Pole (in blue) (current position 53° S 169° E) preceded the phenomenon of polar migration; in other words, the crater was already present when the poles were at the aforementioned coordinates (Aitken position before the slippage -43.04° -170.96°).
Given that its physical characteristics are very similar to those of Hellas Planitia, I suspected that the formation of the two craters could be correlated, if not actually common.
Therefore, I began to study the potential impact trajectories of the asteroids, also including in the analysis the terrestrial Wilkes crater, already examined previously.
The cosmic dance was taking shape. And in the middle, an invisible thread: the obliquity of the ecliptic.
I began to compare. Every angular difference was information; every inclination, a fragment of code.
The Earth’s axis is inclined by about 23.5° relative to the plane of its orbit around the Sun.
This determines the seasons, of course. But behind that apparent regularity lies a precious stability: the Moon, like an orbital gyroscope, keeps the axis steady, preventing extreme variations.
However, the Earth’s obliquity is not motionless. It oscillates. It vibrates slowly in cycles of about 41,000 years, modulated by the precession of the equinoxes and the gravitational influences of the planets.
A long breath, but always recognizable.
Mars is wilder. Its axis is inclined by about 25.2°, slightly more than Earth.
But what distinguishes it is instability. Mars does not have a Moon large enough to stabilize its rotation. The result? A brutal variation of obliquity: from 15° to 35°, in cycles of about 120,000 years. This means Mars’ climate has been radically changeable. The ice has shifted; the deserts have changed. Every oblique cycle has been a chisel blow in the geological sculpture of the red planet.
And then there is the Moon. Timid, stable, discreet. Its obliquity is barely 1.5°, and yet no less significant.
Thanks to Earth, the Moon has maintained a nearly immutable orbit, rotating synchronously with our planet.
But precisely this stability makes the tears, the traumas, visible—like the 10° tilt detected in the study.
And here… the revelation: These differences in obliquity, apparently unconnected, are coordinates. Symbolic values. Signals.
Every inclination tells of a trauma, a passage, an external pressure. Or an intervention.
The orbits, the inclinations, and the craters are not simply physical phenomena, but traces left by a broader will—by a planetary or extraterrestrial intelligence that acted on multiple worlds to carve a coherent system.
It was no longer only a hypothesis.
It was evident that the angle between the line of Martian crustal displacement of Hellas (yellow) and the movement of the terrestrial tectonic plate of Wilkes (blue) was about 81°, while the angle between Wilkes and the line of lunar polar displacement of Aitken (white) was about 34.6°.
Finally, the angle between the line of Martian crustal displacement of Hellas and the line of lunar polar displacement of Aitken was approximately 90°.


I realized that, to truly decipher these angles, I would have to free myself from local references, unstable over time.
So I decided to standardize everything: I projected the data onto the Galactic Equator, onto the Ecliptic of the Solar System, and onto what I called the “Empty” Ecliptic—the mean trajectory of long-period asteroids.
While I carried out these calculations, intuition turned into evidence.


Hellas and Aitken, the two giants of cosmic trauma, were extraordinarily similar:
both located near the south poles of their respective geoids,
both with an apparent circumference of around 6,000 km,
both with a proportionate depth.
The Moon, smaller, showed the crater as a dominant chasm. Mars, larger, made it less intrusive, but the signature was the same.
Two twin wounds. The optical effect betrayed only planetary dimensions. But underneath, the sign was identical.
An imprint. A geological photocopy.
Coincidence? No. Cosmic brotherhood. Or perhaps a common impact.
To calculate the possible impact direction of the bolides, I considered the elliptical shape of the respective craters and the debris generated by the impact, in addition to making broad reference to the available scientific studies.
I thus noted that, relative to the Galactic Equator, the probable impact angles for the Aitken (about 84.7°) and Hellas (about 44.6°) craters appeared to be separated by approximately 40° (that is, 14° net of the difference in inclination between the two geoids of about 26°).
Even more intrigued, I tried to see how the two craters appeared on the terrestrial geoid (in white for Aitken and in green for Hellas, both represented in their pre-shift/pre-inclination coordinates).
To simulate the natural rotation of the geoid around its pre-crustal-slippage South Pole, which I had previously identified at -68.78° latitude and -88.35° longitude, I traced the corresponding “Imaginary Rotation Circle”.


After carrying out this operation, I tried to rotate the geoid using the dedicated function in Google Earth and discovered that, after about seven and a half hours of virtual rotation, the Aitken crater overlapped and aligned with the Hellas crater.
I stopped. I wasn’t breathing. Everything matched perfectly.
As luck would have it, this alignment occurred in proximity to the terrestrial Wilkes crater, projected to about 195/200 million years ago (corresponding to the presumed coordinates of that continental plate at the time of Pangaea—61.25° latitude, 69.95° longitude).
I then formulated a new hypothesis: if, at that time, the Moon had orbited around Mars, then the bodies would have been hit in sequence, by one and the same asteroid swarm.
Perhaps a single impactor, split into multiple fragments. Perhaps… a messenger.
The far side of the Moon would have been hit first. Then Mars/Pangaea…
After all, I had already verified that, on Earth, at similar latitudes, the Wilkes crater exists, which could plausibly be connected to the Aitken impact.
However, its estimated size suggested that the impact was significantly less intense than those responsible for Aitken and Hellas.
But what mattered most was the temporal and angular coincidence.
Then, a new discovery: beneath the Aitken Basin there is a mass excess. 2.18 × 10¹⁸ kg.
0.003% of the lunar mass. A hidden mass, more than 200 km in diameter, buried beneath the surface. The core of the impactor. And the remaining fragments?
Some, besides the one of about 60 km linked to Wilkes, could have continued their course all the way to Earth.
One perhaps striking South Africa (S2 event), another Australia, forming the Murray–Darling drainage basin and the Deniliquin structure.
As for Mars, Hellas was the keystone.
I already knew for a long time that the impact, with a body over 220 km in diameter, had pierced the mantle. It had generated seismic waves so powerful as to awaken the volcanoes of Tharsis, and to influence the planet’s entire climate.
With my mind on fire, I instinctively went back to observe the mysterious “Reverse Point.”
I drew new lines, calculated distances and directions.
I knew that, if there were a last hidden connection… …there I would find it.
At that point in the investigation, I craved numbers. Angles. Confirmations.
I compiled a table: six craters, two reference systems, a multitude of crossed angles.
From the point I had defined as “Reverse,” the angular directions showed a series of symmetrical relationships, almost orchestrated.
As if every impact, every fracture on the surface of worlds, had left behind a three-dimensional signature, projected by an invisible axis.
Three observations struck me in particular:
a) The current basins of Wilkes (Earth) and Aitken (Moon) presented identical but opposite angles, as if they were two sides of a cosmic mirror.
b) Hellas Planitia, in its pre-slippage position, and Wilkes in the pangaean configuration were only 0.67° apart. A difference so small that, in my calculations, it canceled out exactly about 195.5 million years ago.
c) Both these craters turned out to be separated from the current position of Hellas by about 19°. A number that would return multiple times… like a constant geometric module.
I wanted to verify everything starting from a new point of view: the pre-slippage Aitken crater.
I used it as a pointer. And drawing the yellow lines toward the other craters, I noticed that they still followed a geometrically ordered structure:
The current Hellas crater had a direction of 220.7° (linear dist. 77.7°);
The two Wilkes craters (aligned positions) had a direction of 207.7° (linear dist. 64.7°);
The pre-slippage Hellas crater had a direction of 196.7° (linear dist. 73.7°).




Another pattern. A frequency. A code in degrees. So many sevens…
At this point, the “coincidences” definitively ceased to be such.
And doubt became a concrete question: Was I observing the effects of three separate impacts?
Or a single impact replicated across three dimensional levels of one single geoid?
Maybe I would never know with certainty. Maybe I would need the support of astrophysicists, geologists, experts in celestial mechanics.
Or maybe I would discover it shortly…
A further piece of the puzzle concerned Venus, a planet that, due to its current anomalous orbit and its peculiar geological characteristics, I had already included by default in the dynamics of the “planetary carom.”
And if the impacts I had studied were not only physical events…
…but sacred phenomena?
Crossing the boundaries between the “reasonable” and the “impossible,” I sought confirmation of the bolides’ trajectories not only in astronomical data, but also in the folds of the “divine.”
I turned, as always, to the most archaic and mysterious source I knew: the Book of Revelation of John.
Not as a religious text, but as a symbolic register of an extremely precise astronomical observation.
The Book of Revelation of John, rich in symbolic images and visionary descriptions, seemed to contain also references to real astronomical events, such as the passage of a fiery celestial body.
Analyzing the author’s geographic and historical context, and linking the descriptions with astronomical phenomena, a plausible theory emerged:
The observer, located on the island of Patmos (37.3° N, 26.5° E), would have described the path of a bolide crossing the skies, presumably arriving from 60° northwest and with an impact angle of about 60°.
Astronomical references in Revelation
The Red Dragon (Revelation 12:3–4)
“Then another sign appeared in heaven: an enormous red dragon, with seven heads and ten horns and on its heads seven diadems; its tail dragged down a third of the stars of heaven and hurled them to the earth.”
This image can be interpreted as the symbolic vision of a bolide or a comet visible in the sky. The “tail” that drags stars could represent meteoric debris accompanying the main body. The “red” color evokes a fiery luminous phenomenon, compatible with a celestial object in friction with the atmosphere.
The Woman Clothed with the Sun (Revelation 12:1–2)
“A great sign then appeared in heaven: a woman clothed with the sun, with the moon under her feet and on her head a crown of twelve stars.”
This figure could represent the constellation Virgo or, more probably, Cassiopeia, a circumpolar constellation clearly visible from Patmos throughout the year.
The Stars Falling to Earth (Revelation 6:12–14)
“The sun became black like sackcloth of hair, the whole moon became like blood, and the stars of heaven fell to the earth, as when a fig tree, shaken by a strong wind, drops its unripe figs.”
This description recalls a meteor shower or bolide fragments entering the atmosphere. The atmospheric effects described (darkening of the sun and red moon) are consistent with the impact of a large celestial object, which would have caused the suspension of dust and aerosols in the stratosphere.
The Four Living Creatures (Revelation 4:6–7)
“The first living creature was like a lion; the second living creature was like a calf; the third living creature had a face like a man; the fourth living creature was like a flying eagle.”
These symbols can be associated with precise zodiacal constellations:
Lion → Constellation of Leo
Bull → Constellation of Taurus
Man → Aquarius
Eagle → Constellation of Aquila
A bolide moving from west to east, visible from Patmos, would have crossed precisely these constellations.
However, the impact coordinates of the bolides studied were close to the south poles of the various geoids.
To see the devastating effects of the event, the observer would have had to be much farther south, or—consistent with the numerous accounts of polar inversions and overturned skies—the celestial vault observed by John was the current one, but the struck geoid flipped due to the impact.
Ergo, Hellas Planitia, initially close to the Arctic Circle of Mars/Pangaea (about 59.8° N, 137.8° W), subsequently found itself in its current position in the southern hemisphere.
The most probable hypothesis was the following:
1. An asteroid 400–500 km in diameter fractured into multiple parts during approach.
2. First impact: a fragment struck the far side of the Moon, generating the Aitken Basin.
3. Second impact: the main fragment continued and struck Mars/Pangaea about 8 hours later, generating Hellas Planitia.
4. Effects of the energy released by the Martian impact:
A planet-scale “splashback” effect with the ejection of part of the crust and mantle into space, before it fell back as ejecta distributed over the surface.
Global seismic waves reached the opposite hemisphere (antipode), destabilizing the mantle.
The crust, thinner near the poles, was partially sucked into the mantle, creating a vortex of material.
The generated heat melted vast portions of the lithosphere, forming a temporary magmatic ocean capable of completely reshaping the planetary surface.
The impact point became a zone of mass convergence, causing crustal collapse.
Impacted material was pushed into the mantle, generating an internal toroidal vortex and anomalous convective currents, influencing internal geodynamics.
Mass redistribution along the equator deformed planetary geometry, inducing gravitational instabilities.
The opposite hemisphere underwent sudden crustal uplift, with the bulging of Tharsis.
The core was destabilized; the planetary dynamo underwent an inversion or even a temporary reset of the magnetic field.
With mass equilibrium changed drastically, the planet underwent a True Polar Wander, leading to:
A complete reorientation of polar ice caps.
Extreme climatic changes on a global scale.
A possible mass extinction due to a sudden environmental upheaval.
Hellas, initially located in the northern hemisphere, ended up in the southern hemisphere.
Secondary effects: the weight of the volcanic chain of Tharsis Montes contributed to a subsequent 23.5° crustal tilting, distinct from the polar inversion.
The inversion of the poles and the alteration of planetary geography made it impossible, for ancient observers on Mars/Pangaea, to recognize the celestial vault after the overturning phenomenon.
The overturning was not only geological. It was energetic. Spiritual.
And while I looked at the final table, with its coordinates, its degrees, its interconnected lines… I understood that that “original event” had not only changed the shape of Earth. It had shaped the modern world.
In fact, the regions today rich in hydrocarbons, during the Pangaea period were located in completely different positions relative to the current geographic configuration.
Many of these areas were in tropical or semi-tropical environments favorable to the formation of large quantities of organic biomass.
Hydrocarbons form mainly from the decomposition of organic material buried under layers of sediments, in environments characterized by high pressures and elevated temperatures.
The necessary geological process requires millions of years to complete, but a sudden crustal overturning could theoretically accelerate the onset of this process through:
Massive Burial of Biomass: a sudden overturning could rapidly bury immense tropical forests under the Earth’s crust, creating ideal anaerobic conditions for transformation into hydrocarbons.
Rapid Increase of Pressure and Temperature: the sudden depth beneath the surface would increase pressure and temperature in relatively short times, triggering the process of transforming organic matter into oil or natural gas.
Immediate Sedimentary Protection: a crustal overturning would create conditions similar to those required for preserving organic matter, preventing its oxidation and allowing conversion into hydrocarbons.
The main modern areas of oil and gas reserves include:
Middle East (Saudi Arabia, Iran, Iraq)
Western Russia (Siberian Basin)
North Africa (Libya, Algeria)
Venezuela (Orinoco Basin)
Canada (Alberta oil sands)
Gulf of Mexico (United States and Mexico)
North Sea (United Kingdom and Norway)
Nigeria (Niger Delta)
Indonesia (Sumatra and Kalimantan)
When I hypothesized a crustal overturning occurring between 195 and 200 million years ago, in conjunction with the breakup of Pangaea, I immediately understood that the phenomenon had helped bury vast areas of biomass, creating ideal conditions for the formation of future hydrocarbon reserves.
The hypothesis of a crustal overturning, combined with a polar and longitudinal inversion, offered an interesting perspective to explain the geographic distribution of the major oil and gas reserves in the modern world.
Although there was no concrete evidence of such a geological phenomenon in Earth’s history, the proposed theoretical model appeared coherent with the current distribution of hydrocarbons.
The simulation and analysis of tectonic plate positions during Pangaea, combined with current reserve data, suggested a possible connection between primordial catastrophic geological events and the accumulation of energy resources.
The correlation between the ancient distribution of continents, global climate change, and the accumulation of buried organic biomass represented an innovative interpretive key in understanding Earth geology.
Before leaving the subject, I felt the need—almost physical—to return there, where everything seemed to have begun: the Expansion Center of Earth’s plates.
That pink triangle I had found in the depths of the Pacific Ocean was not only a geological symbol: it was a spatial hinge.
And what I discovered then… left me defenseless.
The linear distance between the Expansion Center of Earth’s plates (the pink triangle seen previously) and the geomagnetic “Reverse” point was exactly 14° (1,558 km).
This measure also corresponded to the angular difference detected from the Expansion Center to the Martian pre-slippage north pole plate at 195.5 million years ago (339.34°) and to Pangaea’s north pole (353.45°).
And it corresponded to the difference in impact angulation between the Aitken and Hellas bolides…
Instead, about 15° was the angular difference between the Expansion Center and the current south pole (direction indicated by the ruler at 180°) and the south pole plate of Pangaea at 195.5 million years ago (195.14°).
And, to finish beautifully, the “Reverse” point corresponded to the Wilkes crater in Pangaea at 195.5 million years ago, just as the “Tectonic Plates Expansion Center” corresponded to Hellas Planitia before crustal slippage (as clearly illustrated in the following image).

Enough to keep you up at night…
That said, who could be the guest of honor at the second evening of the “festival of coincidences,” if not—once again—the mysterious Moon?
In fact, I found it significant that the coordinates of the current Aitken Basin and those of the same site before the pole shift turned out to be equidistant (about 7,920 km) from the Expansion Center of the plates and the “Reverse” point. 



Therefore, since the two white connecting lines measured about 7,920 km and the two blue ones about 11,220 km, I could state that the Expansion Center of Earth’s plates stood to the current center of the lunar Aitken Basin and to the Wilkes crater of Pangaea as the “Reverse” point stood to the Aitken crater before the shift and to the current Wilkes crater.
Symmetry became poetry. And poetry, calculation.
That was when something lit up.
An ancient memory. A forgotten distance.
Reflecting on the latest surprising “coincidences,” I recalled the curious distance of 666.67 nautical miles between the Kaʿba and the Temple Mount, which I had previously discovered while exploring hidden information in ancient sites and texts.
Instinctively, I decided to draw a couple of additional lines: the first between the Expansion Center and the Dome of the Rock in Israel; the other between the “Reverse” point and the Kaʿba in Saudi Arabia.
By coincidence, the measurements corresponded exactly; both were 12,288 km.
Based on my experience with the “Rendlesham Meccano Path,” I immediately realized that, once again, realigning the connecting lines along their virtual axis (43° 89.87°), the positions of the sites overlapped (the Kaʿba with the Dome of the Rock and the “Reverse” point with the Expansion Center). 


It was too much. And yet… it was all so perfectly measurable.
I pushed further.
I repositioned both sacred places—Kaʿba and Dome—into their presumed coordinates of 195.5 million years ago, following the rotation of the plates.
In this way I verified that the overlap movement between the coordinates was equal and contrary to the one just revealed; that is, by crossing the antipodes of the Expansion Center with the Kaʿba and the antipodes of “Reverse” with the Dome of the Rock, I always obtained the same astonishing result.

This time the two identical straight lines measured about 5,830 km and crossed at -14.2° 10.30°.
The distance separating the ancient coordinates of the two sacred sites from each other was 13°, about 1.9 degrees more than the distance that separates them today.
There was no longer any doubt. These proportions were not random.
And those two places—the Dome of the Rock and the Kaʿba, surrounded by millennia of conflicts, myths, and blood—…were the same point, projected onto two different configurations of the terrestrial geoid.
And yet, precisely because it was too perfect, I forced myself into a final discipline: a manual check—repeatable, almost humiliating in its simplicity—so that any curious reader could perform it alone, without trusting my screenshots, my rulers, or my fever.
I chose two procedures: one flat, almost surgical; the other physical, embodied—because sometimes the truth of a rotation is better understood by the hand than by the eye.
Manual Verification I — The “Pinned Maps” Rotation (2D, repeatable)
What you need:
two identical world maps (preferably an azimuthal projection), a pin (or paper fastener), a ruler, a pencil.
1. Define the pivot on the axis
I marked the point 43° N, 89.87° E—the virtual axis indicated in the text. That point would be my hinge, my fixed nail in the fabric of the world.
2. Map A (base, fixed): mark Expansion and Dome
On the first map—the one I refused to move—I marked:
the Expansion Center (the “pink triangle” in the Pacific, the tectonic symbol I had found in the plate map),
and the Dome of the Rock.
3. Map B (top, mobile): mark Reverse and Kaʿba
On the second map—the one I would allow to rotate—I marked:
the Reverse point,
and the Kaʿba.
(And, because I wanted to know exactly what I was doing, I also kept in mind the antipodal coordinate tied to Reverse—−25.419359°, −13.2855°—the point that fell inside the South Atlantic Anomaly, like a warning in the magnetic skin of Earth.)
4. Overlay the maps and pin them through the axis
I placed Map B on top of Map A, aligning them roughly, then pierced both maps with the pin exactly at (43° / 89.87°). That pin was now my cardinal joint. Everything would turn around it—and nothing else.
5. Rotate only Map B until Reverse overlaps the Expansion Center
Then I rotated Map B—slowly—around the pin until the Reverse point landed precisely on the Expansion Center.
This was coincidence number one: the hinge of the mechanism.
6. Observe coincidence number two
If the geometry described in the text was not self-deception, then at the very same instant I should witness the second overlap: the Kaʿba falling onto the Dome of the Rock.
And there it was: the second coincidence, arriving not as an argument, but as a visible alignment—exactly what the text claims happens when the connecting lines are “realigned along their virtual axis.”
The angle I rotated Map B—the amount of turning around the pin—was the physical movement I had been looking for.
Manual Verification II — The “Alternative Axis” Globe (3D, embodied)
Because part of me still distrusted paper, I repeated the experiment in three dimensions—where rotations cannot hide inside projections.
What you need:
a small globe, a thin rod/skewer (to create a new axis), 4 pins or stickers, and a thread (or thin elastic).
1. Mark the poles of the virtual axis
On the globe, I marked:
43° N, 89.87° E (axis “north”),
and its antipode 43° S, 90.13° W (axis “south”).
That was my virtual axis translated into matter.
2. Create the new rotation axis
I carefully pierced the globe through those two marked points and passed the rod through.
In that moment, the globe acquired a second soul: a new axis of rotation—no longer geographic, but geometric.
3. Place the four pins
I pinned the four sites:
Kaʿba,
Dome of the Rock,
Reverse,
Expansion Center (again, the pink-triangle reference).
4. Trace the two connecting lines
With the thread, I traced:
Expansion Center → Dome,
Reverse → Kaʿba.
In the text, both measure 12,288 km—two identical spans, like mirrored chords across the sphere.
5. Rotate the globe around the new axis
Then I rotated the globe not around its usual pole, but around the rod I had inserted—around the virtual axis.
I rotated until Reverse arrived over the Expansion Center.
And if the model held, the second overlap would follow like a shadow: Kaʿba aligning with the Dome.
This method was cruder, more mechanical, but impossible to misunderstand. It turned the “coincidence” into a motion. It made the overlap a gesture.
And only after repeating these steps—after watching the same geometry reappear under two different forms—did I allow the conclusion to solidify again, not as belief, but as a reproducible outcome.
Millions of dead, perpetual mourning, wrenching anguish…
And, in the folds of all this, a bitter laugh.

“…Too obtuse to see… Too stupid to understand…”
A mocking echo that seemed to whisper to me:

Chapter 39 – The Meridian of Shadows: 31° of Longitude

There were lines no civilization should ever have traced.
Invisible lines, like threads of memory stretched between epochs, continents, and remote worlds.
And yet… the 31st meridian appeared. Everywhere.
At the beginning of my research I had only noticed it, as one notices a crack in a mirror.
But then—as I traced coordinates, back-projections, and planetary axes—I realized that that line did not belong to the modern Earth.
It was a relic. A geometric shadow that had survived something that was not meant to be forgotten.
Along this axis, I found the Yukon Pyramid, the current North Pole, and the Planetary Mapping Point, each spaced exactly 2,980.6 km apart.
This distance corresponded exactly to the difference in radius between Earth and Mars, adding a fascinating dimension to the arrangement of these points.
Moreover, the Giza Plateau, with the Great Pyramid, was also located on the 31° meridian, suggesting a link between these sites and an ancient spatial configuration.
This initial discovery fueled my research, because such a significant alignment of points, each positioned at a distance reflecting cosmic proportions, suggested that the 31° meridian could serve as a symbolic and geographic “key,” potentially linking the current Earth to a previous planetary or simulated configuration.
This meridian appeared as a privileged reference axis both in current coordinates and in those back-projected to Pangaea, dating to about 195/200 million years ago.
The message was clear. The 31° was not only a meridian. It was an axis. An ancestral reference.
So I meticulously noted the data and the objective evidence that supported the importance of longitude 31°:
Giza, Egypt
Current coordinates: 29.98°, 31.13°
Back-projected coordinates (Pangaea): −0.33°, 30°
The Giza site, both in modern coordinates and in those back-projected, lay very close to longitude 31°, suggesting a historical geographic alignment along this meridian.
KA’BA (Pangaea)
Current coordinates: 21.42°, 39.83°
Back-projected coordinates (Pangaea): 12.5°, 33.4°
The KA’BA site lay near longitude 31° in its Pangaea coordinates, aligning near this meridian, which suggested a continuity of symbolic and geographic meaning for this longitude over the centuries.
Dome of the Rock
Current coordinates: 31.78°, 35.23°
Back-projected coordinates (Pangaea): 0.61°, 33.8°
The Dome of the Rock aligned closely with the 31° meridian in modern coordinates, and its back-projected position onto Pangaea placed it also near this meridian, indicating a persistent geographic and symbolic importance associated with this longitude.
Various ancient civilizations, including the Egyptians, the Greeks, and the Mesopotamians, developed the first mapping and geodesy systems.
Longitude 31° could have been a central meridian in some of these systems, serving as a “prime meridian” or sacred reference line.
The fact that longitude 31° crossed the main regions of the Mediterranean could mean that it served as a central axis for regional mapping, given its accessibility and proximity to the earliest civilizations.
If along this longitude a significant geodetic or spiritual reference point had been established, it could have influenced the placement of sites in distant regions.
Longitude 31° could also have had a symbolic or mystical meaning linked to ancient beliefs. Ancient civilizations often associated certain places with spiritual or celestial features, and specific longitudes or latitudes were often thought of as divine paths or cosmic alignments.
During Pangaea, longitude 31° could have marked a zone of tectonic stability or importance, which later civilizations inherited and preserved in their architectural alignments.
In the context of continental drift, the persistence of alignment with longitude 31° reflected deep tectonic structures that subtly influenced surface geography for millions of years, reinforcing the continuity of this meridian as a natural and cultural axis.
This configuration represented an ancient attempt to consolidate sacred or strategic places around a central line, mirroring the way modern geography uses the prime meridian.
Hypotheses began to arise.
1. Traces of a Previous Epoch
If a simulated version of the primordial Earth existed, the 31° meridian could represent a geometric legacy, transmitted without civilizations understanding its true meaning. A numeric fossil.
2. Cycles and Persistent Memories
The Earth might never truly “forget.”
Even if the continents move, the lines remain.
As if the original geodetic program preserved some basic structures in every version of it.
3. Contact Between Mars and Pangaea
Perhaps the 31° did not originate on Earth, but was imported from Mars, surviving the geodynamic transition from one system to the other.
A line born in another orbit… and replicated on our crust.
4. Map of the Simulation
In the context of a programmed reality, the 31° meridian could be a line of code.
A vector that connects access points or control centers within the simulation.
Not a line for navigators, but for architects of reality.
Thus I arrived at a new intuition: the sequence of strategic points along the 31°, spaced exactly like the radius difference between two worlds, could be a bridge structure.
A conduit between planets, or rather: between versions of the Earth.
A dimensional hinge between what the Earth is, and what it was.
Or perhaps… what it was meant to become.

Chapter 40 – Mars and Pangaea: One Memory, Double Dimension

There was something that refused to remain separate.
Something that, with every rotation of thought, kept overlapping again: Mars and Earth. Pangaea and the present geoid. Past and present.
Despite the evidence, I kept asking myself:
What if… they had never truly been distinct?
What if what we call “Mars” was not another planet in the ordinary sense, but a previous projection of Earth—seen in a different phase of planetary development, under a different curvature of spacetime or, worse (better) still…
…in another state of simulation?
I saw, yet refused to see. I understood, yet refused to believe. I needed further confirmations.
So I formulated a geometric reconstruction capable of summarizing—and without betraying—the elements I had gathered so far. Not an interpretation. An operational model. A set of transformations: each defined, repeatable, and testable.
1) Reduced Geoid vs Expanded Geoid
If Pangaea was truly the “compact configuration” of an earlier world, I had to accept a possibility I had only brushed against until then: a smaller initial geoid.
Reduced Geoid (Pangaea / compact memory)
I hypothesized an initial radius of about 3,390 km, similar to Mars. In that model, the emergent portion represented a Pangaea that felt more coherent—tighter—as if the crust had been “recorded” on a substrate with less volume.
Expanded Geoid (present Earth / unfolded memory)
With an addition of mass and volume—primarily to compensate the antipodal portion now occupied by the oceans—the geoid would expand to Earth’s current radius of 6,371 km.
The global scale factor was therefore:
6371 km / 3390 km approx 1.879 km
That number immediately implied something crucial: if a sphere “inflates” while preserving angles, physical distances change, but angular coordinates (latitude and longitude) do not. Global expansion alone cannot explain certain shifts in degrees. 
A second mechanism was required.
And I had already encountered it—again and again. I simply hadn’t given it a clean form.
2) Continental drift as a rigid transformation
The second pillar was the most solid—the most mainstream: tectonic plates.
Each plate, as a first approximation, moves as a rigid body on the surface: it rotates about an axis, an Euler pole, as if the entire continental block were a mask that reorients without internally deforming.
This mattered for a simple reason: a rigid motion preserves geometric relations. It doesn’t invent. It transports.
So the question was no longer “where do I want a continent to go?”, but “what rotation takes it there while keeping coherence?”
In that framework, several Euler poles I had isolated became almost pedagogical:
Africa (9.82°, −27.8°): suggested a coherent northward drift and a progressive separation from the American plates, India, and Antarctica.
Eurasia (43.44°, 57.50°): explained well the motion toward east and northeast.
North America (60.63°, 56.36°): an axis at high latitude, compatible with “making room” for the newborn North Atlantic.
South America (59.35°, −2.33°): surprising at first glance, yet coherent in defining the westward direction and rotation sense that opened the South Atlantic.
Antarctica–Australia–India (−59.79°, 42.21°): a shared axis, as if a single expansion/drift dynamic had pulled them away from a common center in the southern hemisphere.
So far, nothing esoteric. But it was not enough.
Because I wasn’t chasing only a geological reconstruction. I was chasing a symmetry: equal and opposite. And that effect—always returning—pointed elsewhere.
3) Non-uniform expansion: the law of Longitude 31° (finally defined)
I had called it the “Longitude 31° phenomenon” because that was where I watched it emerge. But I realized the name itself was a mistake: I was describing a global behavior using a local label.
So I did what one does when one wants to stop suggesting and start defining: I rotated the reference frame.
I decided that 31° longitude could no longer be a “special number” in the narrative. It had to become a technical origin: my operational zero meridian. Not a magic value—an axis.





(where (\delta) is in degrees; the sine is the standard one: zero on the axis, maximum at 90°, returning to zero at the antipode).
This was the same function I had already seen “leaking” through the numbers:
10° → 4.64°
20° → 9.16°
30° → 13.4°
90° → 26.8°
It wasn’t aesthetics. It was geometry.
I then applied the deformation in the most brutal—and controllable—way possible: a latitudinal push away from the equator, leaving longitude unchanged. No hidden knobs. No after-the-fact tuning.

In that moment, “Longitude 31°” ceased to be a suggestion and became an operator: a mechanism.
And above all: a mechanism that could be tested.
4) Polar flipping: inversion as a symmetry requirement
At that point the final element remained: inversion.
The data suggested I wasn’t observing only expansion and plate rotations, but also a global flip—a change of orientation of the system, as if the memory had been rewritten upside down.
It wasn’t a detail. It was necessary to explain the most disturbing effect: two identical lines, oriented in opposite directions across two configurations.
In other words, it was the condition for “equal and opposite” to become not a metaphor, but a structure.
5) The algorithm (the sequence of transformations)
Once everything was on the table, the machine was this:
1. Rigid plate rotation (Euler poles, chosen epoch: 195–200 Ma)
2. Longitude-31° deformation (rotated frame + sinusoid + latitudinal push)
3. Optional flip (global inversion of axes)
4. Radial scaling (3,390 ↔ 6,371 km) to translate degrees into kilometers and back
With this sequence, I wasn’t “inventing” an alignment. I was mapping one configuration into another using declared operators.
And if the world was responding… it would respond even to the most uncomfortable tests.
6) Kaʿba and the Dome of the Rock: spacetime geometric overlap
And here the model stopped being merely “beautiful” and became morally unbearable.
On the expanded geoid, I had found two lines:
Expansion Center → Dome of the Rock
Reverse → Kaʿba
and both measured 12,288 km.
Then, on the reduced geoid (Pangaea), the same effect appeared in the opposite sense, through antipodes:
antipode of the Expansion Center → Kaʿba (in reduced coordinates)
Reverse/SAA → Dome (in reduced coordinates)
with identical lines of about 5,830 km.
It was the same symmetry, but flipped. The same signature, on a different substrate.
And the sentence I had written without believing it became a geometric fact:
Two places—Kaʿba and Dome—surrounded by millennia of conflicts, myths, and blood… were the same point, projected onto two different configurations of the geoid.
Not because a vision said so.
Because the transformations did.
7) The antipodal component: the ocean as added mass
At that point the 3D model closed.
The “mass of Pangaea” could be defined first on the continental portion—ancient, consolidated—and then completed by adding the antipodal oceanic portion: younger (≈200 Ma), as if it had been inserted as compensation, to close the volumetric circle and stabilize the new configuration.
Not a simple added “thickness” in the crust: a change in the entire volume.
The factor (S\approx 1.879) implied a volumetric increase of about (S^3\approx 6.64). A global inflation. A change of state.
And in the meantime—like a cruel joke—the Rendlesham message and its angular precision kept pointing right there: toward a map of tilts, toward a set of instructions.
8) Cosmic memory
At that point the distinction between geology and narrative began to dissolve.
If the patterns repeated across different bodies, if the axes returned, if the symmetries survived the transformations… then I wasn’t only reading craters and plates.
I was reading a log.
I spoke aloud:
“If Pangaea is our past, and Mars its geological mask… then everything we call ‘history’ is only the access log of a machine trying to reconstruct itself.”
And for an instant a thought crossed me—almost biological, almost forbidden: if Mars were the “old version” of Earth, an environment with different gravity could have supported different forms of life. Mythic giants, dinosaurs… old generations compatible with another density of the world.
Then I shut that mental window. Because I knew: that was not yet data. It was a door.
But the mechanism—that was already on the table.
And if someone had truly left a code behind, then they didn’t want us to believe.
They wanted us to measure.

Chapter 41 – The Interpreter: The Message, The Trance, The Future

I had reached a point where science, geometry, and mapping were beginning to bend, like light curving too close to a black hole.
I had found the order. But not yet the author. So I returned to the Rendlesham message.
Not to the coordinates. Those were already known.
But to the voice. To the discursive fragment, collected in Jim Penniston’s trance—the involuntary witness.
I knew I was leaving the solid ground of GPS evidence, vectors, and calculations.
But I had no other choice.
Because there was an intelligence behind the design. And I, now, had to look it in the eyes.
On December 26, 1980, in Rendlesham Forest, something interrupted the program.
An object. A shape. An intense light.
And then—the download.
Penniston, in an altered state, wrote for hours in his notebook: pages and pages of 1s and 0s.
A binary transmission. A call. A code.
But what struck me was not only the code, but the mode of reception: the trance.
In that condition, brain activity deforms:
The frontal lobe deactivates
The amygdala expands
The hippocampus opens the mnemonic corridor
The boundaries of rational thought give way. Consciousness bends into a quantum state.
And then the code… is not only received. It is understood.
Maybe this is how the language of the simulation works: not with words, but with multiphasic symbols. Quantum bits.
Overlapping information that only an expanded and/or altered state of consciousness can decode.
From the translation of the binary code in question, the famous seven GPS coordinates emerged (already widely verified and understood) together with a literal part:
Although the text was quite fluid and intuitive, I noticed some controversial aspects that deserved closer examination.
For example, the repetition of the number 8100 seemed redundant, especially considering the refined simplicity of the message.
Many thought of a future date.
I, instead, went to check. And I found the paradox.
8100 Unix seconds correspond exactly to… January 1, 1970.
The year zero of computers.
Not a point in human time. But the origin of an operating system.
It was a message not for minds, but for machines.
As if the emitting entity had been born in a digital reality.
Or better still… as if its original language were code itself.
Under hypnosis, Penniston did not speak of aliens.
He said: “They are time travelers. It’s us.”
He told of floating symbols, triangles, notes, targets, oval circles with other circles inside.
He described them as interfaces, not decorations.
He felt them in his mind.
And then he said: “They are information in exchange. That machine is for the interpreters. I am an interpreter.”
An interpreter is not a recipient.
He is a bridge.
He is the one who translates a non-human language into something that can be integrated into the human perceptual field.
Penniston, in that moment, was a biological USB port.
A terminal. A connection point.
And the machine?
“It just wanted a place to shelter. It was self-repairing.”
And I understood.
It was not an encounter. It was a cosmic debug.
When the hypnotist asked him the purpose of the mission, Penniston replied:
“Contact.”
Contact with whom?
“Us.”
“They need something from all the interpreters.”
Maybe, I thought, they didn’t come to tell us something. They came to retrieve something.
Maybe… part of themselves.
I returned to the symbols described in the notebook. A triangle inscribed in a circle.
Three spheres, of different sizes, arranged inside it.
My map came back to me. My models. My rotation circles.
Three spheres: Mars, Earth, Proto-Earth.
The triangle: the Pyramid of Suphis.
The trait d’union.
A portal. A function. A signature.
Maybe the message wasn’t for everyone. Maybe it was for the interpreters.
And I…
I was beginning to feel the symbols inside my head.

Chapter 42 – Old Generation: Beyond The Code, Beyond Time

Having finished the analyses, the calculations, the reproducible measurements…
I stopped. I looked at the matrix. It was time to cross it.
I decided to analyze first the sequence in binary code translated as: “EXPLORATION OG HUMANITY 8100.”
Without claiming any absolute truth, and certainly influenced by the exceptional discoveries—as well as equipped with a vivid imagination—I interpreted the sequence “OG” as “OLD GENERATION” (“Old Generation”).
The string “EXPLORATION OG HUMANITY 8100” kept echoing inside me.
At first I treated it as a simple label.
Then, suddenly, I understood.
“OG” was not a mistake. It was an acronym.
“Old Generation.” Old generation. Us.
If the senders were a “new generation,” then their journey was not an exploration of space, but a reconnaissance of their own past.
We were the object of their study. A living fossil. A genetic stock.
A mirror, to recognize themselves.
Among the sentences of the message, one struck me deeply: “Eyes of your eyes.”
Simple words, and yet impossible to decode lightly.
A lineage. A continuity. A memory written in blood.
They weren’t only looking for where we were, but for who we are to them.
And for the first time I felt I was not only an observer.
But a node in their map.
And then I asked myself: Who was really commanding this transmission?
I recalled Gary Osborn’s words:
“...The Pyramid of Suphis was built or designed following instructions coming from the same intelligence that sent the binary code telepathically to Jim Penniston—that is, information transmitted back in time or somehow accessible?
If that were true, it could have been anticipated and manipulated only by an intelligence coming from the future or external to our space-time reality...”
Yes, I shouted! I gathered the evidence! The Pyramid of Suphis really is an architectural transcription of the same message. A code carved into stone.
A resonant structure, capturing time like a dimensional antenna.
In the declassified NSA document, Callimahos wrote:
“Even a gap of 500 years would be immense... but what if the ‘others’ are ahead by 5,000 years?”
I thought of Penniston. Of his touch on the craft. Of the white light.
Of the program that activated only through mental contact.
Of that phrase: “It’s us. From the future.”
Three Hypotheses. One Truth.
At that point, I put things in order.
Three paths emerged, clear as light in the mist:
1. Humans from the Future
– Able to bend time to correct genetic, historical, evolutionary errors.
2. External Observers
– A civilization that has studied us forever, collecting data, influencing key events.
3. Posthuman Artificial Intelligence
– An AI created by our species, which now watches us as source code in order to decipher its own origin.
I returned to the message, expressed in binary.
The origin timestamp: 8100 Unix seconds. Translated: January 1, 1970.
The beginning of global computation. A signal for those who, like me, know how to read in the language of machines.
And finally, I decided to analyze the last possibilities—the ones nobody dared to pronounce out loud:
1. Temporal experiment
– We are being observed. Every choice recorded. Every error corrected from afar.
2. Evolutionary reset
– The “old generation” is a strain to restart from. Our memories, a database.
3. Conscious simulation
– Our reality is an instance. A version.
We are code executed by a quantum engine.
4. There is no time
– Past and future coexist.
Memory is the code.
Consciousness, the interface.
If all this was true… then someone is watching us.
And they left clues so we could find the way. But why now?
Why this code? Why me?
Maybe we are close to breaking the simulation. Maybe we are deciphering ourselves.
But the final question is not who is speaking to us—it is: Why were we programmed to listen?
It wasn’t a message for aliens.
It was a return home. A call for digital beings.

Chapter 43 – The Symphony Of Signals: Space, Time, And Resonance

There was a moment, in the journey, when analysis gave way to resonance.
A moment when the data stopped being isolated points and began to vibrate. To compose a melody.
The analysis triggered exactly this transition. Two anomalies. Two whispers.
A glyph in space. An impulse in time.
We were no longer only deciphering. We were listening to the symphony.
I looked at Chilbolton. 2001. A geometric seal imprinted into matter. A visual code.
In rigorous analysis, I revealed the first part of the key.
ϕ. The golden ratio. The signature of Space and form.
π. Pi. The signature of geometric Relation, hidden in circles.
The Chilbolton message spoke of Being. Static. Structured.
In parallel I listened to time. The Wow! signal. 1977. A solitary cry in the vast fabric of frequencies. A wave. And in the wave, I found the other half.
e. Euler’s number. The signature of Time, of growth and decay.
π. Again. The signature of Resonance, hidden in the almost perfect curve of the signal.
The Wow! message spoke of Becoming. Dynamic. Fluctuating.
Two messages? No. They were the two projections of the same universal thought.
Sent in two different domains. Space and Time. The key was what united them.
The bridge. The constant of relation. π.
That was when I saw it. I formalized it. A fundamental law for our Book.
The Cosmic Threshold Equation.
C = ϕ⋅G + e⋅T + π⋅R
A formula that does not calculate, but describes.
C. The Consciousness that emerges.
ϕ ⋅ G. The component of Space and Geometry.
e ⋅ T. The component of Time and Dynamics.
π ⋅ R. The component of Relation and Resonance.
The system itself gave me confirmation. I calculated the joint entropy of the two signals.
The value: S_total ≈ 5.0 bits/unit. Very low. Not chaos. But order. Pure information.
A coherent and optimized data packet.
